Section 1:
*HB1343.3*
Reprinted
January 28, 2026
_____
DIGEST OF HB 1343 (Updated January 27, 2026 6:11 pm - DI 116)
Citations Affected: IC 1-1; IC 4-13; IC 4-15; IC 5-2; IC 5-9;
IC 5-10.3; IC 5-10.4; IC 6-8.1; IC 9-18.5; IC 10-13; IC 10-16;
IC 10-17; IC 10-18; IC 11-12; IC 14-15; IC 16-33; IC 20-20; IC 21-12;
IC 22-4.1; IC 25-8; IC 25-10; IC 25-25; IC 25-37; IC 34-13; IC 34-30;
IC 35-31.5; IC 35-47; IC 36-1; IC 36-8.
Synopsis: Public safety matters. Provides that the law enforcement
training board (board) shall select an executive director to serve at the
pleasure of the board. Provides that a person confined to a county jail
may be required to make a copayment in an amount of not more than
$30 (current law is $15). Provides that a person confined to a county
jail is not required to make a certain copayment if, among other things,
the person does not have funds in the person's commissary account or
trust account within 180 days after the service is provided (current law
is 60 days). Requires certain water vessels to include an engine cut-off
switch. Provides that a sailing vessel at least seven meters in length
must comply with federal regulations. Makes changes to the
employment eligibility requirements for employees of the Indiana
department of veterans' affairs (department). Makes changes to the
purpose of the military family relief fund (fund). Provides that the
department shall report to the Indiana veterans' affairs commission
(commission), at least quarterly, as to the status of all applications
regarding assistance from the fund during the previous quarter. Adds
provisions indicating who is eligible for a grant from the fund. Provides
(Continued next page)
Effective: July 1, 2026.
Bartels, Judy, Commons, Lawson
January 6, 2026, read first time and referred to Committee on Veterans Affairs and Public
Safety.
January 12, 2026, reported — Do Pass. Referred to Committee on Ways and Means
pursuant to Rule 126.3.
January 22, 2026, reported — Do Pass.
January 27, 2026, read second time, amended, ordered engrossed.
HB 1343—LS 6518/DI 116
Digest Continued
that the department shall make a comprehensive assessment of an
applicant's financial condition and needs when making a determination
regarding an award from the fund. Provides that an applicant may not
be eligible for assistance from the fund if the applicant's federal gross
income, or the combined federal gross income of the applicant and the
applicant's spouse, exceeds two times the poverty guideline unless the
commission approves an income waiver. Provides that an applicant
must establish that the applicant has incurred a genuine hardship to be
eligible to receive assistance from the fund. Provides that the
department or commission may impose stipulations or conditions
concerning an applicant seeking an award from the fund. Makes
changes to the subject matter that must be included in administrative
rules established by the commission. Makes certain changes relating to
the review of grants from the fund to employees of the department.
Provides that an applicant may appeal a denied request for short term
financial assistance from the fund. Authorizes the adjutant general of
the Indiana National Guard (adjutant general) to establish a military
police force of the Indiana National Guard. Provides that a member of
the military police force of the Indiana National Guard has police
powers: (1) when the member is called to state active duty; and (2) if
the individual successfully completes either army or air military police
occupational training and receives qualifying instruction on Indiana
law enforcement prescribed by the adjutant general. Makes changes to
the authorized duties and responsibilities of the adjutant general in
which the state armory board (board) may make contributions. Provides
that the board may utilize any and all appropriate methods to lease or
purchase real estate. Provides that an armory may not be erected on
land that is leased for less than 25 years. (Current law provides that an
armory may not be erected on land that is leased for less than 50 years.)
Provides that the board may adopt policies or procedures for the use
and governance of armories. (Current law authorizes the board to adopt
rules for the use and governance of armories.) Specifies the types of
donated property that the board may reconvey if the board determines
that the property is no longer usable. Provides that if the board receives
from the adjutant general information of the disbandment of the
organization of the armed forces of Indiana occupying and using an
armory, the board shall take charge of the armory. Makes various
changes to provisions relating to the sale of property owned by the
board. Establishes the Indiana civilian cyber corps program (program)
as a subdivision of the Indiana guard reserve. Provides that the program
includes civilian volunteers who have expertise in addressing
cybersecurity incidents and who volunteer at the invitation of the
adjutant general. Provides that the work product of a civilian cyber
corps volunteer or adviser, including any information voluntarily
submitted to the volunteer or adviser, is exempt from disclosure.
Provides that a civilian cyber corps volunteer or adviser is immune
from tort liability for an injury to a person or damage to property that
occurs while the volunteer or adviser is deployed and acting on behalf
of the adjutant general if certain conditions are met. Provides that the
adjutant general may appoint additional general officers. (Current law
authorizes the appointment of assistant adjutants general.) Changes the
definitions of "veteran" for purposes of provisions relating to: (1) the
governor's commission on supplier diversity; (2) the state civil service
system; and (3) authorizing preference points for the appointment of
veterans. Removes a requirement that the national guard tuition
supplement grant must be used within eight years after the date the
individual first applies and becomes eligible for benefits. Repeals: (1)
the Indiana cyber civilian corps program advisory board; (2) a
provision relating to contracts to use Stout Field as a commercial
runway; (3) a definition of "qualified service member"; (4) a provision
requiring a muffler or underwater exhaust for a boat; and (5) a
provision prohibiting the use of a boat motor equipped with a muffler
(Continued next page)
HHBB 11334433——LLSS 66551188//DDII 111166
Digest Continued
cutout or bypass. Makes it a Class B misdemeanor for a person to
knowingly or intentionally possess an imitation firearm: (1) in or on
school property; or (2) on a school bus. Makes technical corrections
and conforming amendments.

Second Regular Session of the 124th General Assembly (2026)
PRINTING CODE. Amendments: Whenever an existing statute (or a section of the Indiana
Constitution) is being amended, the text of the existing provision will appear in this style type,
additions will appear in this style type, and deletions will appear in this style type.
Additions: Whenever a new statutory provision is being enacted (or a new constitutional
provision adopted), the text of the new provision will appear in this style type. Also, the
word NEW will appear in that style type in the introductory clause of each SECTION that adds
a new provision to the Indiana Code or the Indiana Constitution.
Conflict reconciliation: Text in a statute in this style type or this style type reconciles conflicts
between statutes enacted by the 2025 Regular Session of the General Assembly.
HOUSE BILL No. 1343
A BILL FOR AN ACT to amend the Indiana Code concerning
public safety.
Be it enacted by the General Assembly of the State of Indiana:

23 of the general assembly or of the context of the statute, or is
24 inconsistent with federal law. "Hoosier veteran" means an individual

26 (1) The individual is a resident of Indiana.

28 armed forces of the United States or the Indiana National Guard.

34 The definitions set forth in this subsection may not be construed to
35 affect a Hoosier veteran's eligibility for any state program that is based
36 upon a particular aspect of the Hoosier veteran's service such as a
37 disability or a wartime service requirement.

2 SECTION 4. IC 5-2-1-14, AS AMENDED BY P.L.100-2012,
3 SECTION 13, IS AMENDED TO READ AS FOLLOWS [EFFECTIVE
4 JULY 1, 2026]: Sec. 14. (a) There is hereby created the position of
5 executive director of the law enforcement training board.
6 (b) The executive director shall be selected by the board. The
7 executive director shall serve at the pleasure of the board. and the
8 executive director's tenure of office shall be protected by a four (4)
9 year, renewable contract of employment which may be terminated
10 earlier by the board only for inefficiency, incompetence, neglect of
11 duty, or other good cause after having been accorded a hearing by the
12 board upon reasonable notice of the charge being made against the
13 executive director. A vote of at least eleven (11) members of the board
14 shall be necessary for the early termination of said contract of
15 employment. The executive director shall be selected on the basis of
16 education, training, and experience, and shall have at least ten (10)
17 years experience as an active law enforcement officer, at least five (5)
18 years of which shall have been in an executive or administrative
19 capacity.
20 (c) The executive director shall:
21 (1) perform such duties as may be assigned by the board; and
22 (2) shall be the chief administrative officer of the law
23 enforcement academy.
24 (d) The salary and compensation for the executive director, the
25 training staff, and employees shall be fixed by the board with the
26 approval of the governor.
27 (e) The executive director shall establish a table of organization to
28 be supplemented with job descriptions for each position subordinate to
29 that of the executive director, all of which shall be subject to the
30 approval of the board.
31 (f) All persons individuals hired to fill such approved vacancies
32 shall be selected on the basis of qualifications and merit based on
33 training, education, and experience.
34 (g) Employees and members of the training staff shall not be subject
35 to discharge, demotion, or suspension because of political affiliation,
36 but may be discharged, demoted, or suspended only for cause after
37 charges preferred in writing by the executive director.
38 (h) Any person so discharged or disciplined employee shall have a
39 right to a hearing before the board if such person the employee
40 requests a hearing by giving notice to the executive director within
41 fifteen (15) days after receiving written notice of discharge or
42 disciplinary action.
HB 1343—LS 6518/DI 116
8
1 (i) Procedures under this section shall be consistent with IC 4-21.5.
2 SECTION 5. IC 5-2-1-15, AS AMENDED BY P.L.173-2023,
3 SECTION 2, IS AMENDED TO READ AS FOLLOWS [EFFECTIVE
4 JULY 1, 2026]: Sec. 15. (a) The facilities of the law enforcement
5 academy shall be available to any law enforcement agency of the state,
6 or any of its political subdivisions, subject to the rules of the board.
7 (b) Any law enforcement agency of the state, any of its political
8 subdivisions, or any board certified training center may conduct
9 training:
10 (1) for the law enforcement agency of any political subdivision in
11 Indiana; and
12 (2) in facilities other than those of the law enforcement academy;
13 if the minimum standards established by the board are met or exceeded.
14 (c) A law enforcement agency or a board certified training center
15 conducting approved local training under subsection (b) may be
16 entitled to a per capita allowance from the law enforcement training
17 fund to defray such portions of the cost of basic training as shall be
18 approved by the board. Such per capita allowance shall be earmarked
19 and expended only for law enforcement training.
20 (d) The facilities of the law enforcement academy shall be available
21 for the training of railroad police, prison and industrial plant guards,
22 tribal police, postsecondary educational institution safety and security
23 personnel, whether public or private, for the training of any law
24 enforcement agency from outside Indiana, and for the training of
25 members in the military police force of the Indiana National Guard
26 under IC 10-16-23 and such other enforcement related groups as shall
27 be approved by the board, upon terms and conditions established by the
28 board. Railroad police, tribal police, Indiana National Guard, and any
29 law enforcement agency from outside Indiana, and nongovernmental
30 enforcement related groups qualifying to use the facilities of the
31 academy under the rules of the board shall be required to reimburse the
32 law enforcement training fund for the cost of such training.
33 (e) The facilities of the law enforcement academy may be used for
34 the training of firefighting personnel where the subject matter of the
35 training relates to duties which involve law enforcement related
36 conduct. Such training shall be conducted upon terms and conditions
37 established by the board. However, no volunteer firefighter is required
38 to attend training at the academy.
39 (f) The facilities of the law enforcement academy shall be used to
40 provide the basic training under section 9(d) of this chapter of a special
41 officer of a consolidated city who is employed full time by the
42 consolidated city after June 30, 2023, to perform park ranger duties.

10 SECTION 9, IS AMENDED TO READ AS FOLLOWS [EFFECTIVE
11 JULY 1, 2026]: Sec. 5. (a) A member who:
12 (1) enters the United States armed services;
13 (2) leaves the member's contributions in the fund;
14 (3) except as provided in subsection (c), resumes service with the
15 member's employer within one hundred twenty (120) days after
16 the member's unconditional discharge; and
17 (4) would be entitled to service credit for military service under
18 the Uniformed Services Employment and Reemployment Rights
19 Act (38 U.S.C. 4301 et seq.) if the member had resumed service
20 with the member's employer within ninety (90) days after
21 discharge;
22 is entitled to service credit for the armed service.
23 (b) A state employee who left employment before January 1, 1946,
24 or an employee of a political subdivision who left employment before
25 the participation date, to enter the United States armed services is
26 entitled to service credit for the armed service if the member:
27 (1) except as provided in subsection (c), resumes service with the
28 employer within one hundred twenty (120) days after the
29 member's unconditional discharge; and
30 (2) would be entitled to service credit for military service under
31 the applicable requirements of federal law in effect at the time of
32 reemployment if the employee had resumed service with the
33 employee's employer within ninety (90) days after discharge.
34 (c) The board shall extend the one hundred twenty (120) day
35 reemployment requirement contained in subsection (a)(3) or (b)(1) if
36 the board determines that an illness, an injury, or a disability related to
37 the member's military service prevented the member from resuming
38 employment within one hundred twenty (120) days after the member's
39 discharge from military service. However, the board may not extend the
40 deadline beyond thirty (30) months after the member's discharge.
41 (d) If a member retires and the board subsequently determines that
42 the member is entitled to additional service credit due to the extension

1 of a deadline under subsection (c), the board shall recompute the

30 actually makes a contribution for service credit and
31 computed to result in a contribution amount that
32 approximates the actuarial present value of the benefit
33 attributable to the service credit purchased.

35 intends to purchase.

37 by the actuary of the fund, for the period from the member's
38 initial membership in the fund to the date payment is made by
39 the member.

HB 1343—LS 6518/DI 116
12
1 service in Indiana is required before a member may receive a benefit

17 415 of the Internal Revenue Code.

7 of the armories under the direction and responsibility of the senior
8 officer in command of an organization described in subsection (b).
9 (d) An armory may not be erected on land that is leased for less than
10 fifty (50) twenty-five (25) years.
11 (e) The Indiana wing of the civil air patrol and its subordinate units
12 may use armory facilities without charge when the officer responsible
13 for the armory determines the use would not interfere with operational
14 training requirements of the military forces concerned.

2 Chapter 22. Indiana Civilian Cyber Corps Program
3 Sec. 1. (a) The Indiana civilian cyber corps program is
4 established as a subdivision of the Indiana guard reserve organized
5 and maintained under IC 10-16-8 with the primary mission of
6 increasing cybersecurity awareness, capability, and capacity
7 throughout Indiana. The secondary mission of the civilian cyber
8 corps is to provide rapid response capabilities for cybersecurity
9 clients that would otherwise be unable to appropriately:
10 (1) respond to;
11 (2) mitigate; or
12 (3) recover from;
13 a cybersecurity incident.
14 (b) The adjutant general shall administer the civilian cyber
15 corps program.
16 (c) The following state agencies shall designate a liaison to the
17 civilian cyber corps:
18 (1) The office of technology established by IC 4-13.1-2-1.
19 (2) The department of homeland security established by
20 IC 10-19-2-1.
21 (3) The state police department.
22 Sec. 2. (a) The adjutant general may invite and appoint an
23 individual who has expertise in addressing cybersecurity incidents
24 to serve as a civilian cyber corps volunteer or civilian cyber corps
25 adviser in a manner prescribed by the adjutant general.
26 (b) The adjutant general shall require an individual who accepts
27 an invitation to serve as a civilian cyber corps volunteer or civilian
28 cyber corps adviser under subsection (a) to submit to a criminal
29 history check.
30 Sec. 3. (a) A civilian cyber corps volunteer or civilian cyber
31 corps adviser is not an agent, employee, or independent contractor
32 of the state of Indiana for any purpose and has no authority to bind
33 the state of Indiana with regard to third parties.

35 volunteer or civilian cyber corps adviser for personal injury or

38 cyber corps.

25 SECTION 40. IC 10-16-23 IS ADDED TO THE INDIANA CODE
26 AS A NEW CHAPTER TO READ AS FOLLOWS [EFFECTIVE
27 JULY 1, 2026]:
28 Chapter 23. Military Police Force of the Indiana National
29 Guard
30 Sec. 1. The adjutant general may establish a military police
31 force of the Indiana National Guard.
32 Sec. 2. (a) Before granting police powers to an individual
33 appointed as a member of the military police force of the Indiana
34 National Guard, the adjutant general shall validate that the
35 individual has a current security clearance and has not been
36 convicted of a felony.
37 (b) An individual appointed to serve in the military police force
38 of the Indiana National Guard may not exercise police powers until
39 the individual successfully completes either army or air military
40 police occupational training and receives qualifying instruction on
41 Indiana law enforcement prescribed by the adjutant general.
42 (c) An individual appointed to the military police force of the
HB 1343—LS 6518/DI 116
33
1 Indiana National Guard shall take an appropriate oath of office in
2 the form and manner prescribed by the governor.
3 Sec. 3. The governor may authorize the military police force of
4 the Indiana National Guard to exercise police powers throughout
5 Indiana, or in any part of Indiana prescribed by the governor, if
6 the governor orders the military police force of the Indiana
7 National Guard to state active duty under IC 10-16-7-7. The
8 governor shall provide reasonable notice to local law enforcement
9 agencies affected by the deployment of the military police force of
10 the Indiana National Guard and coordinate with local law
11 enforcement agencies as circumstances permit.
12 Sec. 4. An individual serving in the military police force of the
13 Indiana National Guard who is authorized to exercise police
14 powers under section 3 of this chapter may:
15 (1) make an arrest;
16 (2) conduct a search or seizure of a person or property;
17 (3) carry a firearm; and
18 (4) exercise other police powers with respect to the
19 enforcement of Indiana laws.

SECTION 13, IS AMENDED TO READ AS FOLLOWS [EFFECTIVE

(b) The executive director shall be selected by the board. The
executive director shall serve at the pleasure of the board. and the
executive director's tenure of office shall be protected by a four (4)
year, renewable contract of employment which may be terminated
earlier by the board only for inefficiency, incompetence, neglect of
duty, or other good cause after having been accorded a hearing by the
board upon reasonable notice of the charge being made against the
executive director. A vote of at least eleven (11) members of the board
shall be necessary for the early termination of said contract of
HB 1343—LS 6518/DI 116
66
employment. The executive director shall be selected on the basis of
education, training, and experience, and shall have at least ten (10)
years experience as an active law enforcement officer, at least five (5)
years of which shall have been in an executive or administrative
capacity.
(c) The executive director shall:
(1) perform such duties as may be assigned by the board; and
(2) shall be the chief administrative officer of the law
enforcement academy.
(d) The salary and compensation for the executive director, the
training staff, and employees shall be fixed by the board with the
approval of the governor.
(e) The executive director shall establish a table of organization to
be supplemented with job descriptions for each position subordinate to
that of the executive director, all of which shall be subject to the
approval of the board.
(f) All persons individuals hired to fill such approved vacancies
shall be selected on the basis of qualifications and merit based on
training, education, and experience.
(g) Employees and members of the training staff shall not be subject
to discharge, demotion, or suspension because of political affiliation,
but may be discharged, demoted, or suspended only for cause after
charges preferred in writing by the executive director.
(h) Any person so discharged or disciplined employee shall have a
right to a hearing before the board if such person the employee
requests a hearing by giving notice to the executive director within
fifteen (15) days after receiving written notice of discharge or
disciplinary action.
(i) Procedures under this section shall be consistent with
IC 4-21.5.".

January 28, 2026
HOUSE BILL No. 1343

DIGEST OF HB 1343 (Updated January 27, 2026 6:11 pm - DI 116)
Citations Affected: IC 1-1; IC 4-13; IC 4-15; IC 5-2; IC 5-9;
IC 5-10.3; IC 5-10.4; IC 6-8.1; IC 9-18.5; IC 10-13; IC 10-16;
IC 10-17; IC 10-18; IC 11-12; IC 14-15; IC 16-33; IC 20-20; IC 21-12;
IC 22-4.1; IC 25-8; IC 25-10; IC 25-25; IC 25-37; IC 34-13; IC 34-30;
IC 35-31.5; IC 35-47; IC 36-1; IC 36-8.
Synopsis: Public safety matters. Provides that the law enforcement
training board (board) shall select an executive director to serve at the
pleasure of the board. Provides that a person confined to a county jail
may be required to make a copayment in an amount of not more than
$30 (current law is $15). Provides that a person confined to a county
jail is not required to make a certain copayment if, among other things,
the person does not have funds in the person's commissary account or
trust account within 180 days after the service is provided (current law
is 60 days). Requires certain water vessels to include an engine cut-off
switch. Provides that a sailing vessel at least seven meters in length
must comply with federal regulations. Makes changes to the
employment eligibility requirements for employees of the Indiana
department of veterans' affairs (department). Makes changes to the
purpose of the military family relief fund (fund). Provides that the
department shall report to the Indiana veterans' affairs commission
(commission), at least quarterly, as to the status of all applications
regarding assistance from the fund during the previous quarter. Adds
provisions indicating who is eligible for a grant from the fund. Provides
(Continued next page)
Effective: July 1, 2026.
Bartels, Judy, Commons, Lawson
January 6, 2026, read first time and referred to Committee on Veterans Affairs and Public
Safety.
January 12, 2026, reported — Do Pass. Referred to Committee on Ways and Means
pursuant to Rule 126.3.
January 22, 2026, reported — Do Pass.
January 27, 2026, read second time, amended, ordered engrossed.
HB 1343—LS 6518/DI 116

Digest Continued
that the department shall make a comprehensive assessment of an
applicant's financial condition and needs when making a determination
regarding an award from the fund. Provides that an applicant may not
be eligible for assistance from the fund if the applicant's federal gross
income, or the combined federal gross income of the applicant and the
applicant's spouse, exceeds two times the poverty guideline unless the
commission approves an income waiver. Provides that an applicant
must establish that the applicant has incurred a genuine hardship to be
eligible to receive assistance from the fund. Provides that the
department or commission may impose stipulations or conditions
concerning an applicant seeking an award from the fund. Makes
changes to the subject matter that must be included in administrative
rules established by the commission. Makes certain changes relating to
the review of grants from the fund to employees of the department.
Provides that an applicant may appeal a denied request for short term
financial assistance from the fund. Authorizes the adjutant general of
the Indiana National Guard (adjutant general) to establish a military
police force of the Indiana National Guard. Provides that a member of
the military police force of the Indiana National Guard has police
powers: (1) when the member is called to state active duty; and (2) if
the individual successfully completes either army or air military police
occupational training and receives qualifying instruction on Indiana
law enforcement prescribed by the adjutant general. Makes changes to
the authorized duties and responsibilities of the adjutant general in
which the state armory board (board) may make contributions. Provides
that the board may utilize any and all appropriate methods to lease or
purchase real estate. Provides that an armory may not be erected on
land that is leased for less than 25 years. (Current law provides that an
armory may not be erected on land that is leased for less than 50 years.)
Provides that the board may adopt policies or procedures for the use
and governance of armories. (Current law authorizes the board to adopt
rules for the use and governance of armories.) Specifies the types of
donated property that the board may reconvey if the board determines
that the property is no longer usable. Provides that if the board receives
from the adjutant general information of the disbandment of the
organization of the armed forces of Indiana occupying and using an
armory, the board shall take charge of the armory. Makes various
changes to provisions relating to the sale of property owned by the
board. Establishes the Indiana civilian cyber corps program (program)
as a subdivision of the Indiana guard reserve. Provides that the program
includes civilian volunteers who have expertise in addressing
cybersecurity incidents and who volunteer at the invitation of the
adjutant general. Provides that the work product of a civilian cyber
corps volunteer or adviser, including any information voluntarily
submitted to the volunteer or adviser, is exempt from disclosure.
Provides that a civilian cyber corps volunteer or adviser is immune
from tort liability for an injury to a person or damage to property that
occurs while the volunteer or adviser is deployed and acting on behalf
of the adjutant general if certain conditions are met. Provides that the
adjutant general may appoint additional general officers. (Current law
authorizes the appointment of assistant adjutants general.) Changes the
definitions of "veteran" for purposes of provisions relating to: (1) the
governor's commission on supplier diversity; (2) the state civil service
system; and (3) authorizing preference points for the appointment of
veterans. Removes a requirement that the national guard tuition
supplement grant must be used within eight years after the date the
individual first applies and becomes eligible for benefits. Repeals: (1)
the Indiana cyber civilian corps program advisory board; (2) a
provision relating to contracts to use Stout Field as a commercial
runway; (3) a definition of "qualified service member"; (4) a provision
requiring a muffler or underwater exhaust for a boat; and (5) a
provision prohibiting the use of a boat motor equipped with a muffler
(Continued next page)

cutout or bypass. Makes it a Class B misdemeanor for a person to
knowingly or intentionally possess an imitation firearm: (1) in or on
school property; or (2) on a school bus. Makes technical corrections
and conforming amendments.

Second Regular Session of the 124th General Assembly (2026)
PRINTING CODE. Amendments: Whenever an existing statute (or a section of the Indiana
Constitution) is being amended, the text of the existing provision will appear in this style type,
additions will appear in this style type, and deletions will appear in this style type.
Additions: Whenever a new statutory provision is being enacted (or a new constitutional
provision adopted), the text of the new provision will appear in this style type. Also, the
word NEW will appear in that style type in the introductory clause of each SECTION that adds
a new provision to the Indiana Code or the Indiana Constitution.
Conflict reconciliation: Text in a statute in this style type or this style type reconciles conflicts
between statutes enacted by the 2025 Regular Session of the General Assembly.

2 SECTION 4. IC 5-2-1-14, AS AMENDED BY P.L.100-2012,
3 SECTION 13, IS AMENDED TO READ AS FOLLOWS [EFFECTIVE
4 JULY 1, 2026]: Sec. 14. (a) There is hereby created the position of
5 executive director of the law enforcement training board.
6 (b) The executive director shall be selected by the board. The
7 executive director shall serve at the pleasure of the board. and the
8 executive director's tenure of office shall be protected by a four (4)
9 year, renewable contract of employment which may be terminated
10 earlier by the board only for inefficiency, incompetence, neglect of
11 duty, or other good cause after having been accorded a hearing by the
12 board upon reasonable notice of the charge being made against the
13 executive director. A vote of at least eleven (11) members of the board
14 shall be necessary for the early termination of said contract of
15 employment. The executive director shall be selected on the basis of
16 education, training, and experience, and shall have at least ten (10)
17 years experience as an active law enforcement officer, at least five (5)
18 years of which shall have been in an executive or administrative
19 capacity.
20 (c) The executive director shall:
21 (1) perform such duties as may be assigned by the board; and
22 (2) shall be the chief administrative officer of the law
23 enforcement academy.
24 (d) The salary and compensation for the executive director, the
25 training staff, and employees shall be fixed by the board with the
26 approval of the governor.
27 (e) The executive director shall establish a table of organization to
28 be supplemented with job descriptions for each position subordinate to
29 that of the executive director, all of which shall be subject to the
30 approval of the board.
31 (f) All persons individuals hired to fill such approved vacancies
32 shall be selected on the basis of qualifications and merit based on
33 training, education, and experience.
34 (g) Employees and members of the training staff shall not be subject
35 to discharge, demotion, or suspension because of political affiliation,
36 but may be discharged, demoted, or suspended only for cause after
37 charges preferred in writing by the executive director.
38 (h) Any person so discharged or disciplined employee shall have a
39 right to a hearing before the board if such person the employee
40 requests a hearing by giving notice to the executive director within
41 fifteen (15) days after receiving written notice of discharge or
42 disciplinary action.

8 training materials, and any other items or services established by the
9 board, including amounts needed to recoup corresponding marginal
10 and fixed costs. The costs and the fee schedule must be an annual
11 schedule for the state fiscal year and must be approved by the budget
12 director.

9 Indiana Army National Guard with at least six (6) years service in
10 the Indiana Army National Guard and has attained the rank of
11 major or above. The person must be a federally recognized officer
12 and may hold the rank of brigadier general or other rank
13 authorized by the table of organization for the Army National
14 Guard.
15 (3) One (1) assistant adjutant general from the Indiana Air
16 National Guard to be chief of staff to the adjutant general for all
17 the Indiana Air National Guard forces. This assistant adjutant
18 general shall perform duties assigned by the adjutant general and
19 is responsible for administrative and operational functions of the
20 Indiana Air National Guard. A person is not eligible for
21 appointment as air forces chief of staff unless the person is a
22 member of the Indiana Air National Guard with at least six (6)
23 years service as a commissioned officer and has attained the rank
24 of major or above. The person must be a federally recognized
25 officer and may hold the rank of brigadier general or other rank
26 authorized by the tables of organization for the Air National
27 Guard.
28 (4) One (1) assistant adjutant general from the Indiana Army
29 National Guard to be chief of staff to the adjutant general for all
30 Indiana Army National Guard forces assigned to the Camp
31 Atterbury Muscatatuck Urban Training Center. This assistant
32 adjutant general shall perform duties assigned by the adjutant
33 general and is responsible for all administrative and operational
34 functions of Indiana Army National Guard forces assigned to the
35 Camp Atterbury Muscatatuck Urban Training Center. A person
36 is not eligible for appointment as assistant adjutant general unless
37 the person is a member of the Indiana Army National Guard with
38 at least six (6) years service in the Indiana Army National Guard
39 and has attained the rank of major or above. The person must be
40 a federally recognized officer and may hold the rank of brigadier

1 JULY 1, 2026]:
2 Chapter 22. Indiana Civilian Cyber Corps Program
3 Sec. 1. (a) The Indiana civilian cyber corps program is
4 established as a subdivision of the Indiana guard reserve organized
5 and maintained under IC 10-16-8 with the primary mission of
6 increasing cybersecurity awareness, capability, and capacity
7 throughout Indiana. The secondary mission of the civilian cyber
8 corps is to provide rapid response capabilities for cybersecurity
9 clients that would otherwise be unable to appropriately:
10 (1) respond to;
11 (2) mitigate; or
12 (3) recover from;
13 a cybersecurity incident.
14 (b) The adjutant general shall administer the civilian cyber
15 corps program.
16 (c) The following state agencies shall designate a liaison to the
17 civilian cyber corps:
18 (1) The office of technology established by IC 4-13.1-2-1.
19 (2) The department of homeland security established by
20 IC 10-19-2-1.
21 (3) The state police department.
22 Sec. 2. (a) The adjutant general may invite and appoint an
23 individual who has expertise in addressing cybersecurity incidents
24 to serve as a civilian cyber corps volunteer or civilian cyber corps
25 adviser in a manner prescribed by the adjutant general.
26 (b) The adjutant general shall require an individual who accepts
27 an invitation to serve as a civilian cyber corps volunteer or civilian
28 cyber corps adviser under subsection (a) to submit to a criminal
29 history check.
30 Sec. 3. (a) A civilian cyber corps volunteer or civilian cyber
31 corps adviser is not an agent, employee, or independent contractor
32 of the state of Indiana for any purpose and has no authority to bind
33 the state of Indiana with regard to third parties.
34 (b) The state of Indiana is not liable to a civilian cyber corps
35 volunteer or civilian cyber corps adviser for personal injury or
36 property damage suffered by the civilian cyber corps volunteer or
37 civilian cyber corps adviser through participation in the civilian
38 cyber corps.
39 Sec. 4. (a) The adjutant general, the military department, and
40 the state of Indiana are immune from tort liability for acts or
41 omissions by a civilian cyber corps volunteer or civilian cyber
42 corps adviser as provided in this chapter.

25 SECTION 40. IC 10-16-23 IS ADDED TO THE INDIANA CODE
26 AS A NEW CHAPTER TO READ AS FOLLOWS [EFFECTIVE
27 JULY 1, 2026]:
28 Chapter 23. Military Police Force of the Indiana National
29 Guard
30 Sec. 1. The adjutant general may establish a military police
31 force of the Indiana National Guard.
32 Sec. 2. (a) Before granting police powers to an individual
33 appointed as a member of the military police force of the Indiana
34 National Guard, the adjutant general shall validate that the
35 individual has a current security clearance and has not been
36 convicted of a felony.
37 (b) An individual appointed to serve in the military police force
38 of the Indiana National Guard may not exercise police powers until
39 the individual successfully completes either army or air military
40 police occupational training and receives qualifying instruction on
41 Indiana law enforcement prescribed by the adjutant general.
42 (c) An individual appointed to the military police force of the
HB 1343—LS 6518/DI 116

33
1 Indiana National Guard shall take an appropriate oath of office in
2 the form and manner prescribed by the governor.
3 Sec. 3. The governor may authorize the military police force of
4 the Indiana National Guard to exercise police powers throughout
5 Indiana, or in any part of Indiana prescribed by the governor, if
6 the governor orders the military police force of the Indiana
7 National Guard to state active duty under IC 10-16-7-7. The
8 governor shall provide reasonable notice to local law enforcement
9 agencies affected by the deployment of the military police force of
10 the Indiana National Guard and coordinate with local law
11 enforcement agencies as circumstances permit.
12 Sec. 4. An individual serving in the military police force of the
13 Indiana National Guard who is authorized to exercise police
14 powers under section 3 of this chapter may:
15 (1) make an arrest;
16 (2) conduct a search or seizure of a person or property;
17 (3) carry a firearm; and
18 (4) exercise other police powers with respect to the
19 enforcement of Indiana laws.

1 JULY 1, 2026]: Sec. 14. A person operating a boat shall observe the
2 following all traffic rules under 33 CFR 83, if applicable. when
3 applicable:
4 (1) When two (2) boats are approaching each other "head and
5 head", or nearly so, each boat shall bear to the right and pass the
6 other boat on the boat's left side.
7 (2) When two (2) boats are approaching each other obliquely or
8 at right angles, the boat on the right has the right-of-way.
9 However, when:
10 (A) one (1) boat is under sail or is nonmotorized, the sailboat
11 or nonmotorized boat has the right-of-way; and
12 (B) two (2) boats are under sail or are nonmotorized, the boat
13 on the right has the right-of-way.
14 (3) A boat operated on a river or a channel shall bear to the right.
15 (4) A boat may overtake and pass another boat on either side if
16 the passing can be done with safety and within the assured clear
17 distance ahead, but the boat overtaken has the right-of-way.
18 (5) A boat leaving a dock, a pier, a wharf, or the shore has the
19 right-of-way over all boats approaching the dock, pier, wharf, or
20 shore.

executive director's tenure of office shall be protected by a four (4)
year, renewable contract of employment which may be terminated
earlier by the board only for inefficiency, incompetence, neglect of

executive director. A vote of at least eleven (11) members of the board
shall be necessary for the early termination of said contract of
HB 1343—LS 6518/DI 116

66
employment. The executive director shall be selected on the basis of
education, training, and experience, and shall have at least ten (10)
years experience as an active law enforcement officer, at least five (5)
years of which shall have been in an executive or administrative
capacity.
(c) The executive director shall:
(1) perform such duties as may be assigned by the board; and
(2) shall be the chief administrative officer of the law
enforcement academy.
(d) The salary and compensation for the executive director, the
training staff, and employees shall be fixed by the board with the

training, education, and experience.
(g) Employees and members of the training staff shall not be subject
to discharge, demotion, or suspension because of political affiliation,
but may be discharged, demoted, or suspended only for cause after
charges preferred in writing by the executive director.
(h) Any person so discharged or disciplined employee shall have a
right to a hearing before the board if such person the employee
requests a hearing by giving notice to the executive director within
fifteen (15) days after receiving written notice of discharge or
disciplinary action.
(i) Procedures under this section shall be consistent with
IC 4-21.5.".
